283→// Otherwise, it is derived from the lowercase name of the field.\n   284→func fieldKey(field reflect.StructField) string {\n   285→\tif tag := field.Tag.Get(\"mapstructure\"); tag != \"\" {\n ...string) []string {\n   340→\tfor _, vs := range v {\n   341→\t\tif vs != \"\" {\n   342→\t\t\ts = append(s, vs)\n   343→\t\t}\n   344→\t}\n   345→\n   346→\treturn s\n   347→}\n   348→\n   349→// bind invokes the supplied function \"fn\" with each possible set of\n   350→// prefixes for the next prefix (\"next\").\n   351→// If the last prefix is \"*\" then we must search the current environment\n   352→// for matching env vars to obtain the potential keys which populate\n   353→// the unbound map keys.\n   354→func bind(env, prefixes []string, next string, fn func([]string)) {\n   355→\t// given the previous entry is non-existent or not the wildcard\n   356→\tif len(prefixes) < 1 || prefixes[len(prefixes)-1] != wildcard {\n   357→\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(prefixes, next))\n   358→\t\treturn\n   359→\t}\n   360→\n   361→\t// drop the wildcard and derive all the possible keys from\n   362→\t// existing environment variables.\n   363→\tp := make([]string, len(prefixes)-1)\n   364→\tcopy(p, prefixes[:len(prefixes)-1])\n   365→\n   366→\tvar (\n   367→\t\t// makezero linter doesn't take note of subsequent copy\n   368→\t\t// nolint https://github.com/ashanbrown/makezero/issues/12\n   369→\t\tprefix = strings.ToUpper(strings.Join(append(p, \"\"), \"_\"))\n   370→\t\tkeys   = strippedKeys(env, prefix, strings.ToUpper(next))\n   371→\t)\n   372→\n   373→\tfor _, key := range keys {\n   374→\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(p, strings.ToLower(key), next))\n   375→\t}\n   376→}\n   377→\n   378→// strippedKeys returns a set of keys derived from a list of env var keys.\n   379→// It starts by filtering and stripping each key with a matching prefix.\n   380→// Given a child delimiter string is supplied it also trims the delimeter string\n   381→// and any remaining characters after this suffix.\n   382→//\n   383→// e.g strippedKeys([\"A_B_C_D\", \"A_B_F_D\", \"A_B_E_D_G\"], \"A_B\", \"D\")\n   384→// returns [\"c\", \"f\", \"e\"]\n   385→//\n   386→// It's purpose is to extract the parts of env vars which are likely\n   387→// keys in an arbitrary map type.\n   388→func strippedKeys(envs []string, prefix, delim string) \"\" {\n\t\ttag, attr, ok := strings.Cut(tag, \",\")\n\t\tif !ok || attr == \"squash\" || attr == \"omitempty\" {\n\t\t\treturn tag\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn strings.ToLower(field.Name)\n}\n\ntype envBinder interface {\n\tMustBindEnv(...string)\n}\n\n// bindEnvVars descends into the provided struct field binding any expected\n// environment variable keys it finds reflecting struct and field tags.\nfunc bindEnvVars(v envBinder, env, prefixes []string, typ reflect.Type) {\n\t// descend through pointers\n\tif typ.Kind() == reflect.Pointer {\n\t\ttyp = typ.Elem()\n\t}\n\n\tswitch typ.Kind() {\n\tcase reflect.Map:\n\t\t// recurse into bindEnvVars while signifying that the last\n\t\t// key was unbound using the wildcard \"*\".\n\t\tbindEnvVars(v, env, append(prefixes, wildcard), {\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor structField := range typ.Fields() {\n\t\t\tkey := fieldKey(structField)\n\n\t\t\tbind(env, prefixes, key, func(prefixes []string) {\n\t\t\t\tbindEnvVars(v, env, prefixes, structField.Type)\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tbind(env, prefixes, \"\", func(prefixes []string) {\n\t\tv.MustBindEnv(strings.Join(prefixes, \".\"))\n\t})\n}\n\nconst wildcard = \"*\"\n\nfunc appendIfNotEmpty(s []string, v ...string) []string {\n\tfor _, vs := range v {\n\t\tif vs != \"\" {\n\t\t\ts = append(s, vs)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// bind invokes the supplied function \"fn\" with each possible set of\n// prefixes for the next prefix (\"next\").\n// If the last prefix is \"*\" then we must search the current environment\n// for matching env vars to obtain the potential keys which populate\n// the unbound map keys.\nfunc bind(env, prefixes []string, next string, fn func([]string)) {\n\t// given the previous entry is non-existent or not the wildcard\n\tif len(prefixes) < 1 || prefixes[len(prefixes)-1] != wildcard {\n\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(prefixes, next))\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// drop the wildcard and derive all the possible keys from\n\t// existing environment variables.\n\tp := make([]string, len(prefixes)-1)\n\tcopy(p, prefixes[:len(prefixes)-1])\n\n\tvar (\n\t\t// makezero linter doesn't take note of subsequent copy\n\t\t// nolint https://github.com/ashanbrown/makezero/issues/12\n\t\tprefix = strings.ToUpper(strings.Join(append(p, \"\"), \"_\"))\n\t\tkeys   = strippedKeys(env, prefix, strings.ToUpper(next))\n\t)\n\n\tfor _, key := range keys {\n\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(p, strings.ToLower(key), next))\n\t}\n}\n\n// strippedKeys returns a set of keys derived from a list of env var keys.\n// It starts by filtering and stripping each key with a matching prefix.\n// Given a child delimiter string is supplied it also trims the delimeter string\n// and any remaining characters after this suffix.\n//\n// e.g strippedKeys([\"A_B_C_D\", \"A_B_F_D\", \"A_B_E_D_G\"], \"A_B\", \"D\")\n// returns [\"c\", \"f\", \"e\"]\n//\n// It's purpose is to extract the parts of env vars which are likely\n// keys in an arbitrary map type.\nfunc strippedKeys(envs []string, prefix, delim string) (keys []string) {\n\tfor _, env := range envs {\n\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(env, prefix) {\n\t\t\tenv = env[len(prefix):]\n\t\t\tif env == \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif delim == \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, env)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// cut the string on the child key and take the left hand component\n\t\t\tif left, _, ok := strings.Cut(env, \"_\"+delim); ok {\n\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, left)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn\n}\n\n// getFliptEnvs returns all environment variables which have FLIPT_\n// as a prefix. It also strips this prefix before appending them to the\n// resulting set.\nfunc getFliptEnvs() (envs []string) {\n\tconst prefix = \"FLIPT_\"\n\tfor _, e := range os.Environ() {\n\t\tkey, _, ok := envs\n}\n\nfunc (c *Config) validate() error {\n\tif c.Version != \"\" {\n\t\tif strings.TrimSpace(c.Version) != Version {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"invalid version: %s\", The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.\n\nCockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.\n\n## Overview\n\nThe implementation involves:\n1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`\n2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`\n3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver\n4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB\n5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n6. Updating testing infrastructure\n7. Analytics table with PostgreSQL-compatible schema\n- `002_create_table_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Aggregated analytics table\n- `003_create_view_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - View for aggregated data\n\nUse standard PostgreSQL DDL syntax (no MergeTree, Enum, or ClickHouse-specific features).\n\n### 5. **Configuration Schemas**\n- **`config/flipt.schema.cue`**: Add `cockroachdb` section to `#analytics.storage` with `enabled` and `url` fields\n- **`config/flipt.schema.json`**: Will be regenerated from CUE schema\n\n### 6. **Testing Infrastructure** (`internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go`)\n- Update `Open()` function to detect and support both ClickHouse and CockroachDB based on environment or config\n- Add CockroachDB container setup function (similar to ClickHouse)\n- Update `newMigrator()` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n- Support both database types in test setup\n\n### 7. **Server Initialization** (`internal/cmd/grpc.go`)\n- Add conditional branch for CockroachDB in analytics initialization\n- Import CockroachDB client (will be created from ClickHouse pattern)\n- Initialize CockroachDB client when enabled in config\n- Register with analytics server\n\n### 8. **Configuration Tests** (`internal/config/analytics_test.go`)\n- Add `TestAnalyticsCockroachDBConfiguration()` test\n- Verify CockroachDB config parsing\n- Test validation logic\n\n### 9. **CockroachDB Client** (`internal/server/analytics/`)\n- Can initially reuse/adapt existing ClickHouse client or create new package\n- Implement methods for flag evaluation counting using PostgreSQL SQL syntax\n- Handle time-series aggregation with PostgreSQL functions\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Core Infrastructure\n1. Add `CockroachDB` to `Driver` type and `stringToDriver` map in `db.go`\n2. Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB connections using PostgreSQL driver\n3. Add CockroachDB configuration to `analytics.go`\n4. Create CockroachDB migration files under `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`\n\n### Phase 2: Migration & Validation\n1. Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2328,"cache_read_input_tokens":63396,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2328},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ce5baff8-67cc-43e8-b91f-d10dae7ec328","uuid":"8aa361e3-f9da-4245-ae76-458bdf3bc335"}

The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.\n\nCockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.\n\nCockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.\n\n## Overview\n\nThe implementation involves:\n1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`\n2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`\n3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver\n4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB\n5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n6. Updating testing infrastructure\n7. Integrating CockroachDB into the gRPC server initialization\n\n## Files to Modify\n\n### 1. **Core Driver System** (`internal/storage/analytics/db.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDB` constant to the `Driver` type\n- Update `stringToDriver` map to include `\"cockroachdb\": CockroachDB`\n- Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB configuration\n- Import PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB connections\n\n### 2. **Configuration** (`internal/config/analytics.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` struct with `Enabled` and `URL` fields\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` field to `AnalyticsStorageConfig`\n- Add `Options()` method to `CockroachDBConfig` (parse PostgreSQL DSN)\n- Update `String()` method to return \"cockroachdb\" when enabled\n- Update `setDefaults()` to set default values for CockroachDB config\n- Update `validate()` method to validate CockroachDB URL and buffer settings\n- Update `Enabled()` method to check CockroachDB enabled status\n\n### 3. **Migration System** (`internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go`)\n- Import PostgreSQL migration driver from golang-migrate\n- Update `expectedVersions` map to add `CockroachDB: 3`\n- Update `NewMigrator()` function to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL driver\n- Use PostgreSQL migration driver instance for CockroachDB\n\n### 4. **Migration Files** (`internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`)\nCreate three pairs of up/down migration files:\n- `001_create_table_counter_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Analytics table with PostgreSQL-compatible schema\n- `002_create_table_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Aggregated analytics table\n- `003_create_view_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - View for aggregated data\n\nUse standard PostgreSQL DDL syntax (no MergeTree, Enum, or ClickHouse-specific features).\n\n### 5. **Configuration Schemas**\n- **`config/flipt.schema.cue`**: Add `cockroachdb` section to `#analytics.storage` with `enabled` and `url` fields\n- **`config/flipt.schema.json`**: Will be regenerated from CUE schema\n\n### 6. **Testing Infrastructure** (`internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go`)\n- Update `Open()` function to detect and support both ClickHouse and CockroachDB based on environment or config\n- Add CockroachDB container setup function (similar to ClickHouse)\n- Update `newMigrator()` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n- Support both database types in test setup\n\n### 7. **Server Initialization** (`internal/cmd/grpc.go`)\n- Add conditional branch for CockroachDB in analytics initialization\n- Import CockroachDB client (will be created from ClickHouse pattern)\n- Initialize CockroachDB client when enabled in config\n- Register with analytics server\n\n### 8. **Configuration Tests** (`internal/config/analytics_test.go`)\n- Add `TestAnalyticsCockroachDBConfiguration()` test\n- Verify CockroachDB config parsing\n- Test validation logic\n\n### 9. **CockroachDB Client** (`internal/server/analytics/`)\n- Can initially reuse/adapt existing ClickHouse client or create new package\n- Implement methods for flag evaluation counting using PostgreSQL SQL syntax\n- Handle time-series aggregation with PostgreSQL functions\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Core Infrastructure\n1. Add `CockroachDB` to `Driver` type and `stringToDriver` map in `db.go`\n2. Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB connections using PostgreSQL driver\n3. Add CockroachDB configuration to `analytics.go`\n4. Create CockroachDB migration files under `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`\n\n### Phase 2: Migration & Validation\n1. Update `migrator.go` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n2. Add expected version for CockroachDB migrations\n3. Update configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n4. Add configuration validation tests\n\n### Phase 3: Testing & Integration\n1. Update testing infrastructure to support CockroachDB\n2. Add CockroachDB client package (adapt from ClickHouse)\n3. Update server initialization code\n4. Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n"}},{"tool_name":"ExitPlanMode","tool_use_id":"toolu_01AnGQPMyGHyiCbyiU1SeHQB","tool_input":{"plan":"# CockroachDB Analytics Backend Implementation Plan\n\n## Context\n\nFlipt currently supports ClickHouse and Prometheus as analytics storage backends, but not CockroachDB despite its PostgreSQL-compatible wire protocol. The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.\n\nCockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.\n\n## Overview\n\nThe implementation involves:\n1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`\n2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`\n3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver\n4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB\n5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n6. Updating testing infrastructure\n7. Integrating CockroachDB into the gRPC server initialization\n\n## Files to Modify\n\n### 1. **Core Driver System** (`internal/storage/analytics/db.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDB` constant to the `Driver` type\n- Update `stringToDriver` map to include `\"cockroachdb\": CockroachDB`\n- Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB configuration\n- Import PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB connections\n\n### 2. **Configuration** (`internal/config/analytics.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` struct with `Enabled` and `URL` fields\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` field to `AnalyticsStorageConfig`\n- Add `Options()` method to `CockroachDBConfig` (parse PostgreSQL DSN)\n- Update `String()` method to return \"cockroachdb\" when enabled\n- Update `setDefaults()` to set default values for CockroachDB config\n- Update `validate()` method to validate CockroachDB URL and buffer settings\n- Update `Enabled()` method to check CockroachDB enabled status\n\n### 3. **Migration System** (`internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go`)\n- Import PostgreSQL migration driver from golang-migrate\n- Update `expectedVersions` map to add `CockroachDB: 3`\n- Update `NewMigrator()` function to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL driver\n- Use PostgreSQL migration driver instance for CockroachDB\n\n### 4. **Migration Files** (`internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`)\nCreate three pairs of up/down migration files:\n- `001_create_table_counter_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Analytics table with PostgreSQL-compatible schema\n- `002_create_table_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Aggregated analytics table\n- `003_create_view_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - View for aggregated data\n\nUse standard PostgreSQL DDL syntax (no MergeTree, Enum, or ClickHouse-specific features).\n\n### 5. **Configuration Schemas**\n- **`config/flipt.schema.cue`**: Add `cockroachdb` section to `#analytics.storage` with `enabled` and `url` fields\n- **`config/flipt.schema.json`**: Will be regenerated from CUE schema\n\n### 6. **Testing Infrastructure** (`internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go`)\n- Update `Open()` function to detect and support both ClickHouse and CockroachDB based on environment or config\n- Add CockroachDB container setup function (similar to ClickHouse)\n- Update `newMigrator()` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n- Support both database types in test setup\n\n### 7. **Server Initialization** (`internal/cmd/grpc.go`)\n- Add conditional branch for CockroachDB in analytics initialization\n- Import CockroachDB client (will be created from ClickHouse pattern)\n- Initialize CockroachDB client when enabled in config\n- Register with analytics server\n\n### 8. **Configuration Tests** (`internal/config/analytics_test.go`)\n- Add `TestAnalyticsCockroachDBConfiguration()` test\n- Verify CockroachDB config parsing\n- Test validation logic\n\n### 9. **CockroachDB Client** (`internal/server/analytics/`)\n- Can initially reuse/adapt existing ClickHouse client or create new package\n- Implement methods for flag evaluation counting using PostgreSQL SQL syntax\n- Handle time-series aggregation with PostgreSQL functions\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Core Infrastructure\n1. Add `CockroachDB` to `Driver` type and `stringToDriver` map in `db.go`\n2. Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB connections using PostgreSQL driver\n3. Add CockroachDB configuration to `analytics.go`\n4. Create CockroachDB migration files under `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`\n\n### Phase 2: Migration & Validation\n1. Update `migrator.go` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n2. Add expected version for CockroachDB migrations\n3. Update configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n4. Add configuration validation tests\n\n### Phase 3: Testing & Integration\n1. Update testing infrastructure to support CockroachDB\n2. Add CockroachDB client package (adapt from ClickHouse)\n3. Update server initialization code\n4. Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n"}},{"tool_name":"ExitPlanMode","tool_use_id":"toolu_013cMQhZ4ozaURBjohDNPxMR","tool_input":{"allowedPrompts":[],"plan":"# CockroachDB Analytics Backend Implementation Plan\n\n## Context\n\nFlipt currently supports ClickHouse and Prometheus as analytics storage backends, but not CockroachDB despite its PostgreSQL-compatible wire protocol.
